الوجود
المجاز
الحقيقة
المماسة
المباينة
المتغايرات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'qiyam' and 'wujud' are interchangeable and equally precise for describing divine attributes.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that 'qiyam' is metaphorical while 'wujud' is literal, making 'wujud' the more accurate term for divine attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, which expression is more accurate for God's knowledge?
A) It subsists by His essence (qa'im bi-dhatihi).
B) It exists by His essence (mawjud bi-dhatihi).
C) It is with Him (ma'ahu).
D) It is in Him (fihi).

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari insisted on using literal terms like 'wujud' for divine attributes and avoided any expression that implies distinctness or relational categories applicable to created things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe Allah's attributes, do you ever use words that slip past your mind without examining whether they imply a limitation? How will you now train your tongue to be as precise as al-Ash'ari insisted?
?
Is there a part of your heart that prefers vague or poetic language about Allah because it feels safer than the exacting truth? What would it cost you to submit to this kind of theological discipline?
?
You have just seen that the words 'with', 'in', 'adjacent', and 'separate' are all unfit for Allah's knowledge. Now think: when you speak of your own relationship to His knowledge—do you treat it as something distinct from Him, or as truly His? If the former, what is your heart actually worshiping?

Three Views on Affirming Divine Knowledge
The author presents three views on the proper expression for God's knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three different expressions used by Ahl al-Hadith, Maturidi scholars, and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi to affirm God's knowledge, and the theological concerns behind each.

Core Idea
How we speak about God's attributes matters—words can imply misconception or protect truth.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla presents three distinct approaches to affirming that Allah is knowing. The differences may seem subtle, but they reflect deep theological caution. The Ahl al-Hadith use 'by knowledge', most Maturidi scholars avoid that phrase to prevent imagining knowledge as a tool, and al-Maturidi himself says 'by essence' to negate any hint of otherness while still affirming attributes. Let's examine each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the Arabic and translation to find the three groups: Ahl al-Hadith, Maturidi scholars (mashayikh), and al-Maturidi. Note their exact wording.
The differences are in the preposition and noun: بعلم, وله علم, بذاته.
2
Understand the rationale of each
For each position, understand why they chose that expression. The Ahl al-Hadith follow literal texts; the Maturidi scholars avoid tool-implication; al-Maturidi avoids otherness.
The passage explains al-Maturidi's intention explicitly.
3
Reflect on the broader debate
The author notes this issue is vast. Why would such a subtle difference cause great debate? Think about how language affects theology.
4
Review the common misunderstanding
Some may think al-Maturidi denied attributes. The passage clarifies he did not. Understand why this misunderstanding arises.
The misconception is explicitly addressed in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن عبارة عامة متكلمي أهل الحديث في هذه المسألة أن يقال: إن الله تعالى عالم بعلم وكذا فيما وراء ذلك من الصفات، وأكثر مشايخنا – رحمهم الله – امتنعوا عن هذه العبارة احترازا عما يوهم أن العلم آلة وأداة فيقولون: الله تعالى عالم وله علم، وكذا فيما وراء ذلك من الصفات. والشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي رحمه الله يقول : إن الله تعالى عالم بذاته قادر بذاته، ولا يريد به نفي الصفات لأنه أثبت الصفات في جميع مصنفاته وأتى بالدلائل لإثباتها ودفع شبهاتهم على وجه لا مخلص للخصوم عن ذلك غير أنه أراد بذلك دفع وهم المغايرة، وأن ذاته تعالى يستحيل أن لا يكون عالما، وهذه مسألة عظيمة كثيرة الشبه جمة الحجج اتسع فيها مجال الجدال، وفسح مكان الصيال وكثر من أرباب النظر وأرباب النحل في فروعها وتوابعها النزاع والخصام وفيما ذكرنا من الحجج ودفع الشبه غنية عما وراء ذلك لمن لم يحد عن سواء الطريق ولم يعدم مواد الهداية والتوفيق. والله الموفق.
Then know that the expression of the generality of the theologians (mutakallimin) among the People of Hadith (ahl al-hadith) in this matter is to say: Allah - exalted is He - is knowing by knowledge, and similarly for other attributes beyond that. And most of our masters (mashayikh) - may Allah have mercy on them - refrained from this expression as a precaution against what suggests that knowledge is an instrument (ala) and a tool (ada). So they say: Allah - exalted is He - is knowing and He has knowledge, and similarly for other attributes beyond that. And Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi - may Allah have mercy on him - says: Allah - exalted is He - is knowing by His essence (bi-dhatihi), powerful by His essence. And he does not intend thereby to negate the attributes, because he affirmed the attributes in all his works and brought proofs for their establishment and refuted the doubts of his opponents in a manner leaving no escape for the adversaries. Rather, he intended thereby to repulse the illusion of otherness (taghayur), and that His essence - exalted is He - is impossible for it not to be knowing. And this is a great issue, abounding in doubts, filled with arguments; the arena of debate has widened and the field of contest has been opened, and many of the people of theoretical inquiry and the people of sects have increased in dispute and wrangling over its branches and consequences. And what we have mentioned of proofs and refutation of doubts suffices beyond that for one who does not deviate from the middle way and is not deprived of the resources of guidance and success. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage presents three positions on how to speak of God's knowledge and attributes. First, the Ahl al-Hadith say 'Allah is knowing by knowledge'. Second, most Maturidi scholars avoid this because it might imply knowledge is an instrument or tool, so they say 'Allah is knowing and He has knowledge'. Third, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi goes further and says 'Allah is knowing by His essence' and 'powerful by His essence', intending to negate the illusion of otherness (taghayur) while still affirming attributes through his works and proofs. The author notes the great scholarly debate on this issue and concludes that the proofs given are sufficient for those who are rightly guided. The passage ends with a prayer for success.

Key Terms
عالم بعلم
آلة وأداة
المغايرة
بذاته
أهل الحديث
المشايخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Maturidi denied the attributes when he said 'by His essence'.
Correction: The passage clarifies he affirmed attributes in all his works and intended to negate otherness, not the attributes themselves.

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Mansur al-Maturidi say 'Allah is knowing by His essence'?
A) To deny that Allah has knowledge altogether.
B) To negate the illusion of otherness (taghayur) while still affirming attributes.
C) To claim that knowledge is identical to the essence without distinction.
D) To reject the Ahl al-Hadith position entirely.

Key Takeaway
The expression of God's attributes must avoid implying imperfection, and al-Maturidi's 'by essence' formulation safeguards against the illusion of otherness while upholding the reality of attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say or hear that 'Allah knows', do you ever unconsciously imagine His knowledge as something He uses, like a tool? How does the Mashayikh's caution against 'آلة وأداة' expose a hidden assumption in your own heart? What will you do to purify your mental image of Allah's attributes?
?
Al-Maturidi said 'by His essence' to repel the illusion of otherness. Have you ever felt a distance—a sense that Allah's attributes are 'things' somehow separate from His reality? How does this lesson call you to a more unified and awe-filled conception of Allah?
?
The author says the proofs given suffice 'for one who does not deviate from the middle way.' Which of the three expressions most resonates with your soul? And more importantly—does your daily speech about Allah reflect that care to avoid misunderstanding, or are you careless with words about your Lord?

The Cautious Phrasing of the Maturidi Majority
Al-Nasafi states the majority Maturidi view and its rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why most Maturidi scholars avoided saying 'God is knowing by knowledge' and preferred 'God is knowing and has knowledge.'

Core Idea
The majority Maturidis guarded against suggesting that divine attributes are like tools.

Al-Nasafi begins by presenting the cautious approach of the majority of Maturidi scholars. They avoided the phrase 'knowing by knowledge' because it could wrongly imply that knowledge is an instrument or tool separate from God. Instead, they affirmed both the attribute and its possession while maintaining tanzih.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to get the gist.
2
Identify the two phrasings
Notice the difference between 'knowing by knowledge' and 'knowing and has knowledge'. What is the reasoning given for avoiding the first?
The text says they refrained 'as a precaution against what might imply that knowledge is a tool and instrument'.
3
Reflect on the theological concern
Consider why implying that knowledge is a tool (آلة وأداة) would be problematic in Islamic theology. This relates to God's transcendence (tanzih).
This cautiousness demonstrates the scholars' carefulness in speech about Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى عالم بعلم وكذا فيما وراء ذلك من الصفات، وأكثر مشايخنا – رحمهم الله – امتنعوا عن هذه العبارة احترازا عما يوهم أن العلم آلة وأداة فيقولون: الله تعالى عالم وله علم، وكذا فيما وراء ذلك من الصفات. - والشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي رحمه الله يقول : إن الله تعالى عالم بذاته قادر بذاته، ولا يريد به نفي الصفات لأنه أثبت الصفات في جميع مصنفاته وأتى بالدلائل لإثباتها ودفع شبهاتهم على وجه لا مخلص للخصوم عن ذلك غير أنه أراد بذلك دفع وهم المغايرة، وأن ذاته تعالى يستحيل أن لا يكون عالما، وهذه مسألة عظيمة كثيرة الشبه جمة الحجج اتسع فيها مجال الجدال، وفسح مكان الصيال وكثر من أرباب النظر وأرباب النحل في فروعها وتوابعها النزاع والخصام وفيما ذكرنا من الحجج ودفع الشبه غنية عما وراء ذلك لمن لم يحد عن سواء الطريق ولم يعدم مواد الهداية والتوفيق. والله الموفق.
He is exalted, knowing by knowledge, and likewise for attributes beyond that. And most of our scholars – may God have mercy on them – refrained from this expression as a precaution against what might imply that knowledge is a tool and instrument, so they say: God exalted is knowing and has knowledge, and likewise for attributes beyond that. – And the Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, may God have mercy on him, says: God exalted is knowing by His essence, powerful by His essence, and he does not intend by that the negation of attributes, because he affirmed the attributes in all his works and brought proofs for their affirmation and repelled their doubts in a manner from which the opponents have no escape, except that he intended by that to repel the illusion of otherness, and that His essence, exalted, is impossible not to be knowing. And this is a great issue, abundant in doubts, plentiful in proofs, in which the arena of debate expanded, the field of dominance widened, and among the people of speculation and the people of sects there was much dispute and contention in its branches and consequences. And in what we have mentioned of proofs and repelling doubts there is sufficiency beyond that for one who does not deviate from the straight path and does not lack the materials of guidance and success. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage presents a nuanced theological argument within the Maturidi school regarding divine attributes. It begins by stating the cautious position of most Maturidi scholars: they avoid saying 'knowing by knowledge' because it might imply that knowledge is a separate instrument or tool (آلة وأداة). Instead, they prefer to say 'God is knowing and has knowledge,' thereby affirming the attribute without implying a tool-like relation. Then it contrasts this with the formulation of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi himself: he says God is knowing by His essence (بذاته) and powerful by His essence. The author immediately clarifies that al-Maturidi does not intend to deny attributes—he indeed affirmed them in his works and provided proofs against opponents. Instead, his intention was to repel the illusion of otherness (وهم المغايرة), meaning the false impression that the attributes are separate from the divine essence. Al-Maturidi argues that it is impossible for God's essence not to be knowing. The passage then reflects on the complexity of this issue, describing it as a great matter (مسألة عظيمة) with many doubts and arguments, leading to extensive debate and disputes among scholars. The author asserts that the proofs and refutations already provided are sufficient for anyone who remains on the straight path. The structure is: first the majority view, then al-Maturidi's view with its interpretation, then a concluding remark on the sufficiency of the evidence.

Key Terms
عالم بعلم
آلة وأداة
الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the majority Maturidis denied that God has knowledge because they avoided saying 'by knowledge'.
Correction: The passage clearly states they affirmed both 'knowing' and 'has knowledge'. Their avoidance was only a linguistic precaution, not a denial of the attribute.

Checkpoint
Why did most Maturidi scholars refrain from saying 'God is knowing by knowledge'?
A) They denied that God has knowledge.
B) They feared it might imply knowledge is an instrument.
C) They followed al-Maturidi's exact phrase.
D) They considered it a heresy.

Key Takeaway
The majority Maturidis avoided the phrase 'knowing by knowledge' to prevent any misconception that divine attributes are like instruments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used casual or careless language when describing God, even without realizing it? What specific phrase will you now be more mindful of?
?
The scholars changed their words to protect God's transcendence. Is your speech about God a reflection of that same care, or have you been negligent? What is one practical way you can guard your tongue starting today?
?
If someone asks you why you say 'God has knowledge' instead of 'God knows by knowledge', will you be able to explain the reason? How can you teach others to speak about God with precision and reverence?

Al-Maturidi's Formulation: Knowing by His Essence
Al-Nasafi presents al-Maturidi's formulation and its correct interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Maturidi's statement that God is knowing by His essence and why it does not deny attributes.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's 'by His essence' repels the illusion of otherness, not negates attributes.

Al-Nasafi then presents the view of the school's founder, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. His phrase 'knowing by His essence' might seem to negate attributes, but al-Nasafi clarifies that al-Maturidi affirmed attributes in all his works. His intention was to avoid the false notion that attributes are distinct entities separate from the divine essence.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Maturidi's statement
Read the Arabic passage from 'والشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي' to the end. Then read the translation.
2
Note the immediate clarification
Al-Nasafi explicitly says al-Maturidi did not intend to negate attributes. He affirmed them and provided proofs. Identify this clarification.
The text says 'ولا يريد به نفي الصفات' (he does not intend by that the negation of attributes).
3
Understand 'wahm al-mughāyara'
The phrase 'دفع وهم المغايرة' means 'to repel the illusion of otherness'. Consider what this illusion is: that attributes are separate entities co-existing with the essence.
Al-Maturidi's formulation emphasizes that God's essence is necessarily knowing, without a separate attribute that is 'other' than the essence.
4
Reflect on the complexity of the issue
Al-Nasafi describes this as a great issue with many doubts and proofs. Note that he considers the evidence sufficient for those on the straight path.
This shows the depth of theological debate on attributes.
